  1. 5 Getting Started [93,696 ms]

    Features 1 1 3

    1. 3 Installing The Framework [5 ms]

      Scenarios 1 2 0 
      As a developer
You can leverage xBDD within your .Net testing projects
By installing the xBDD.Core nuget package

      1. 2 If You Use An MS Test Project [0 ms]

        1. Then you create an MSTest project by following the directions here: https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/dotnet/core/testing/unit-testing-with-mstest [0 ms]
        2. And you can install xBDD by executing: [Input] [0 ms] 
          dotnet add package xBDD

      2. 0 For An Xunit Project [Skipped - Not Started] [2 ms]

      3. 0 For An N Unit Project [Skipped - Not Started] [0 ms]

    2. 2 Executing Your First Scenario [88,095 ms]

      Scenarios 1 0 1 
      As a developer
You can automate a basic scenario
By using xB.AddScenario and the Given, When, Then, and And operations.

      1. 3 Running A Success Web UI Test [43,901 ms]

        1. Given you code the following feature definition: [Input] [0 ms] 
          namespace Amazon.Features.SearchingProducts
{
    using Microsoft.VisualStudio.TestTools.UnitTesting;
    using System;
    using System.Threading.Tasks;
    using xBDD;
    using xBDD.Browser;

	[TestClass]
	[AsA("anonymous user")]
	[YouCan("search across all amazon products")]
	[By("using primary search bar on the home page")]
	public class SearchingAllProducts: IFeature
	{
		private User you = new User();
		public IOutputWriter OutputWriter { get; private set; }

		public SearchingAllProducts()
		{
			OutputWriter = new TestContextWriter();
		}
		
		[TestMethod]
		public async Task SearchWithSearchButton()
		{
			await xB.AddScenario(this)
				.Given(you.NavigateTo("the amazon home page","https://www.amazon.com"))
				.When(you.EnterTheText("echo").In("the search box", "#twotabsearchtextbox"))
				.And(you.Click("the search button", "input[type=submit]"))
				.Then(you.WillSee("the search results section", "#s-results-list-atf").IsVisible())
				.Run();
		}
	}
}
        2. When you run the MS Test Project with the following command: [Input] [Output] [43,883 ms] 
          dotnet test -v n --filter FullyQualifiedName=Amazon.Features.SearchingProducts.SearchingAllProducts.SearchWithSearchButton

  4. 3 Generate Reports - Customize Html Report [5,805 ms]

    Features 3 0 0
    Scenarios 9 0 0

    1. 3 Write Failures Only [348 ms]

      Scenarios 3 0 0 
      As a Developer
You can set the html report to only report on failures
By passing the report writer a true value for the failuresOnly parameter.

      1. 3 Passing [146 ms]

        1. Given the test results of a single passing scenario set to report only failures [1 ms]
        2. When you navigate to the test html report with a single passing scenario [119 ms]
        3. Then you will see the test run areas list is not there [23 ms]

      2. 3 Skipped [94 ms]

        1. Given the test results of a single skipped scenario set to only report on failures [2 ms]
        2. When you navigate to the test html report with a single skipped scenario [67 ms]
        3. Then you will see the test run areas list is not there [24 ms]

      3. 3 Failing [103 ms]

        1. Given the test results of a full test run with all outcomes set to only report on failures [16 ms]
        2. When you navigate to the test html report with a single failed scenario [53 ms]
        3. Then you will see the step 2 with red badge is visible because the step failed and the report will be expanded to the failed step [32 ms]

    2. 3 Shorten Area Name [4,120 ms]

      Scenarios 3 0 0 
      As a Developer
You can shorten the area name in the Html report.
By shorten the area name by removing the beginning of the name that matches a provided string

      1. 4 Matches Start Of Area Name [3,763 ms]

        1. Given the test results of a single passing scenario set to skip the string 'My ' in the area name [4 ms]
        2. When you navigate to the test html report with a single passing scenario [3,656 ms]
        3. Then you will see the area title line is visible [46 ms]
        4. And you will see the area title line has text 'Area 1' [55 ms]

      2. 4 Matches None Of Area Name [182 ms]

        1. Given the test results of a single passing scenario set to skip the string 'No Match' in the area name [2 ms]
        2. When you navigate to the test html report with a single passing scenario [79 ms]
        3. Then you will see the area title line is visible [37 ms]
        4. And you will see the area title line has text 'My Area 1' [63 ms]

      3. 4 Matches All Of Area Name [170 ms]

        1. Given the test results of a single passing scenario set to skip the string 'My Area 1' in the area name [1 ms]
        2. When you navigate to the test html report with a single passing scenario [99 ms]
        3. Then you will see the area title line is visible [26 ms]
        4. And you will see the area title line has text '[Missing! (or Full Name Skipped)]' [42 ms]

    3. 3 Sort Test Run Results [1,330 ms]

      Scenarios 3 0 0 
      As a Developer
You can control the order test results are rendered
By calling the SortTestRunResults method on the test run: 'xB.CurrentRun.SortTestRunResults' before running the html report

      1. 4 Not Sorted [470 ms]

        1. Given a sample executed test run that is not sorted [15 ms]
        2. When you navigate to the sample test html report that is not sorted [313 ms]
        3. Then you will see the feature name has text 'Sample All Outcome Feature' because it was the first feature alphabetically [70 ms]
        4. And you will see the scenario name has text 'Failed Scenario' because it is the first scenario alphabetically [69 ms]

      2. 5 Sorted [408 ms]

        1. Given a sample executed test run that is not sorted [8 ms]
        2. When you navigate to the sample test html report that is sorted [79 ms]
        3. And you click when the feature name is visible [161 ms]
        4. Then you will see the feature name has text 'Sample Passing Feature' because it was the first in the feature sort [Output] [80 ms]

      3. 5 Partially Sorted [444 ms]

        1. Given a sample executed test run that is not sorted [6 ms]
        2. When you navigate to the sample test html report that is sorted [89 ms]
        3. And you click when the feature name is visible [124 ms]
        4. Then you will see the feature name has text 'Sample Skipped Feature' because it was the second in the feature sort [Output] [91 ms]

          using System.Threading.Tasks;
using xBDD.Features;
namespace xBDD.Features.GenerateReports.GenerateTextReport.WriteToTextScenarios
{
    public class SkippedEmptyScenario : IExecute<string>
    {
        public async Task<string> Execute()
        {
            var xBDD = new xBDDMock();
            xBDD.CurrentRun.TestRun.Name = "My Test Run";
            try
            {
                await xBDD.CurrentRun
                    .AddScenario("My Scenario", "My Feature", "My.Area.Path")
                    .Skip("Deferred");
            }
            catch { }
            return await xBDD.CurrentRun.TestRun.WriteToText();
        }
    }
}

      3. 3 Write Run Empty Scenario [3 ms]

        1. Given you code the following feature definition: [Input] [0 ms] 
          using System.Threading.Tasks;
using xBDD.Features;
namespace xBDD.Features.GenerateReports.GenerateTextReport.WriteToTextScenarios
{
    public class RunEmptyScenario : IExecute<string>
    {
        public async Task<string> Execute()
        {
            var xBDD = new xBDDMock();
            xBDD.CurrentRun.TestRun.Name = "My Test Run";
            await xBDD.CurrentRun
                .AddScenario("My Scenario", "My Feature", "My.Area.Path")
                .Run();
            return await xBDD.CurrentRun.TestRun.WriteToText();
        }
    }
}

      4. 3 Write Skipped Scenario With Steps [3 ms]

        1. Given you code the following feature definition: [Input] [0 ms] 
          using System.Threading.Tasks;
using xBDD.Features;
namespace xBDD.Features.GenerateReports.GenerateTextReport.WriteToTextScenarios
{
    public class SkippedScenarioWithSteps : IExecute<string>
    {
        public async Task<string> Execute()
        {
            var xBDD = new xBDDMock();
            xBDD.CurrentRun.TestRun.Name = "My Test Run";
            try
            {
                await xBDD.CurrentRun
                    .AddScenario("My Scenario", "My Feature", "My.Area.Path")
                    .Given(xBDD.CreateStep("my starting condition"))
                    .When(xBDD.CreateStep("my action"))
                    .Then(xBDD.CreateStep("my ending condition"))
                    .Skip("Deferred");
            }
            catch { }
            return await xBDD.CurrentRun.TestRun.WriteToText();
        }
    }
}
        2. When the method is executed [2 ms]
        3. Then the test results written should match the template: [Input] [0 ms] 
          My Test Run

My.Area.Path
	My Feature
		My Scenario [Skipped - Deferred]
			Given my starting condition

      12. 3 Write Run Scenario With Step With Multiline Parameter [3 ms]

        1. Given you code the following feature definition: [Input] [0 ms] 
          using System.Threading.Tasks;
using xBDD.Features;
namespace xBDD.Features.GenerateReports.GenerateTextReport.WriteToTextScenarios
{
    public class RunScenarioWithStepWithMultilineParameter : IExecute<string>
    {
        public async Task<string> Execute()
        {
            var xBDD = new xBDDMock();
            xBDD.CurrentRun.TestRun.Name = "My Test Run";
            await xBDD.CurrentRun
                .AddScenario("My Scenario", "My Feature", "My.Area.Path")
                .Given(xBDD.CreateStep("my starting condition with the following", (s) => { }, $"My{System.Environment.NewLine}multiline{System.Environment.NewLine}parameter"))
                .When(xBDD.CreateStep("my action"))
                .Then(xBDD.CreateStep("my ending condition"))
                .Run();
            return await xBDD.CurrentRun.TestRun.WriteToText();
        }
    }
